1. Creation of Matrix and Special Matrices classes OR Implementation of the different functions of the Matrix and Special Matrices.

12/04/26, 10:51 am - +91 63761 77672: Respected Sir/Ma’am,

We, the undersigned students of MCA First Year, Jamia Millia Islamia, respectfully request the urgent intervention of the Department of Student Welfare in a matter that is now seriously affecting our academic standing, our internships, and our future placement eligibility.

We have been stopped from appearing in Sessional-II on the ground of attendance shortage. However, our grievance is not limited to the fact that we were stopped. The deeper concern is the manner in which this entire process has been handled: the attendance position was not transparently disclosed to us in advance, no meaningful opportunity was given to verify or challenge the figures, and the communication was made at a time when students were effectively prevented from seeking immediate clarification or relief.

Most importantly, the decision was conveyed on a non-working day. By informing students over the weekend, when there was no normal departmental functioning and no office staff available, the affected students were left with no practical way to approach the department, inspect the attendance record, clarify discrepancies, or seek intervention from higher authorities in time. This timing deprived students of any real opportunity to respond before the adverse action took effect. It gave the clear impression that the matter was communicated in a manner that would leave students without any effective remedy.

We are also deeply concerned that the attendance record itself has not been handled transparently. Students were not provided a clear, subject-wise attendance position in time. It was conveyed among students that attendance had earlier been shown by one of the teachers, but this was later stopped, and the records were no longer being properly made available. As a result, students are now being penalized on the basis of figures that they were not given a fair chance to examine or contest. This has created serious confusion, mistrust, and distress.

There is a further concern regarding consistency and fairness. Students have reason to believe that the attendance rule may not have been applied uniformly in all cases, and that some students with low attendance may have been treated differently from others. We are not asking that any allegation be accepted without verification. We are only requesting that the matter be examined impartially so that it may be ensured that attendance-related decisions are being applied equally, fairly, and without arbitrariness.

We also wish to highlight that students in other departments who face attendance shortage are often being given remedial opportunities or alternate academic measures to make up the deficiency or recover missed sessional components. In our case, no such meaningful relief has been extended so far. We are being informally told that there may be a Sessional-III opportunity, but that does not resolve the core issue. If the attendance deficiency itself is not addressed now, the same students may again be told during Sessional-III that their attendance is still short. The same problem may then continue into the main examinations as well. In that event, Sessional-III would not operate as a real remedy at all.

We therefore wish to state clearly that the affected students are fully willing to comply with any reasonable remedial measure that may be permitted. Whether the University considers extra classes, online academic sessions, assignments, tutorials, supervised project work, academic duty, or any other permissible method, we are ready to undertake it in good faith so that our attendance requirement may be fulfilled. We are not seeking exemption from academic responsibility. We are only asking for a fair and workable opportunity to regularize the deficiency, instead of facing repeated debarment without transparency and without any practical path to improvement.

The consequences of this issue are extremely serious for us. Many affected students are currently engaged in or preparing for summer internships, and academic complications or backlogs arising from this situation may directly lead to the loss of those opportunities. Further, MCA is a professional course, and a backlog in the early semesters has severe consequences for future placement eligibility. If any of us receive a backlog in the current second semester, it may effectively shut us out from placement opportunities in the final year. For students in a professional programme, this is not merely an internal academic inconvenience; it can directly affect employability and career prospects.

In view of the above, we most respectfully request that the Department of Student Welfare urgently intervene and ensure the following:

1. Immediate disclosure of the complete subject-wise attendance record of all affected students, including total classes held and total classes attended.
2. Clear written communication of the exact basis on which each student was stopped from appearing in Sessional-II.
3. An impartial review of whether attendance-related decisions have been applied uniformly and fairly across all students.
4. A fair opportunity for students to represent their case before any further adverse action is taken.
5. Immediate consideration of reasonable remedial academic measures through which affected students may fulfill attendance requirements and avoid repetition of the same issue in Sessional-III and in the main examinations.
6. Necessary directions to the department to ensure that attendance is communicated in a timely, transparent, and consistent manner, and not in a way that deprives students of an effective chance to respond.

The affected students are:

* 25MCA005 – Alisha Khanam
* 25MCA016 – Faisal Ansari
* 25MCA017 – Faizan Yousuf
* 25MCA023 – Kunal Chhabra
* 25MCA024 – MD Shahalam Khan
* 25MCA027 – Shahnebaj
* 25MCA028 – Md Muzammil
* 25MCA029 – Md Mozammil Raja
* 25MCA033 – Saad
* 25MCA035 – Hammad
* 25MCA041 – Rahul
* 25MCA044 – Saddam Khan
* 25MCA048 – Shahzan Zafar
* 25MCA052 – Vishwajeet Singh

We therefore request your urgent intervention in the interest of fairness, transparency, and the academic future of the affected students.

Thank you.

Sincerely,
Affected MCA First Year Students
Jamia Millia Islamia

Further, MCA is a professional course, and a backlog in the early semesters has severe consequences for future placement eligibility. If any of us receive a backlog in the current second semester, it may effectively shut us out from placement opportunities in the final year. For students in a professional programme, this is not merely an internal academic inconvenience; it can directly affect employability and career prospects.

Our attendance is affected during Ramzan and during Eid week as most of the students went home. Also some of the students have medical issues due to which they missed out some of the classes.
In view of the above, we most respectfully request that the Department of Student Welfare urgently intervene and ensure the following:

1. Immediate disclosure of the complete subject-wise attendance record of all affected students, including total classes held and total classes attended.
2. Clear written communication of the exact basis on which each student was stopped from appearing in Sessional-II.
3. A fair opportunity for students to represent their case before any further adverse action is taken.
4. Immediate consideration of reasonable remedial academic measures through which affected students may fulfill attendance requirements and avoid repetition of the same issue in Sessional-III and in the main examinations.
6. Necessary directions to the department to ensure that attendance is communicated in a timely, transparent, and consistent manner, and not in a way that deprives students of an effective chance to respond.

The affected students are:

* 25MCA005 – Alisha Khanam
* 25MCA016 – Faisal Ansari
